Question 1easy

Which gas do plants take in to make food during photosynthesis?

  1. Oxygen
  2. Nitrogen
  3. Carbon Dioxide
  4. Hydrogen
Show answer

Answer: Carbon Dioxide

Plants use carbon dioxide (CO2) from air, water from soil, and sunlight to make food (glucose) through photosynthesis.

Question 2easy

What is the speed of light?

  1. 3 × 10^6 m/s
  2. 3 × 10^8 m/s
  3. 3 × 10^10 m/s
  4. 3 × 10^4 m/s
Show answer

Answer: 3 × 10^8 m/s

The speed of light in vacuum is approximately 3 × 10^8 m/s (300,000 km/s).

Question 3easy

What force keeps us on the ground?

  1. Magnetic force
  2. Friction
  3. Gravitational force
  4. Electrical force
Show answer

Answer: Gravitational force

Gravity (gravitational force) is the force of attraction between the Earth and all objects on it. It keeps us grounded.

Question 4easy

Which part of the plant makes food using sunlight?

  1. Roots
  2. Stem
  3. Leaf
  4. Flower
Show answer

Answer: Leaf

Leaves contain chlorophyll (green pigment) and perform photosynthesis to make food using sunlight, CO2, and water.

Question 5easy

What type of energy does the Sun give to Earth?

  1. Mechanical energy
  2. Chemical energy
  3. Nuclear energy
  4. Solar (radiant) energy
Show answer

Answer: Solar (radiant) energy

The Sun releases nuclear energy through fusion reactions, which reaches Earth as solar/radiant energy (light and heat).

Question 6easy

Which vitamin is produced in the body by exposure to sunlight?

  1. Vitamin A
  2. Vitamin B12
  3. Vitamin C
  4. Vitamin D
Show answer

Answer: Vitamin D

Vitamin D is synthesized in the skin when exposed to ultraviolet B (UVB) radiation from sunlight. It is essential for bone health.

Question 7easy

Sound cannot travel through:

  1. Water
  2. Air
  3. Steel
  4. Vacuum
Show answer

Answer: Vacuum

Sound requires a medium (solid, liquid, or gas) to travel. It cannot travel through a vacuum because there are no particles to transmit the vibrations.

Question 8medium

Newton's Second Law of Motion states that Force = :

  1. Mass × Velocity
  2. Mass × Acceleration
  3. Velocity / Time
  4. Mass × Distance
Show answer

Answer: Mass × Acceleration

Newton's Second Law: F = ma (Force = Mass × Acceleration). Greater force = greater acceleration for the same mass.

Question 9medium

The phenomenon of light bending when it passes from one medium to another is:

  1. Reflection
  2. Diffraction
  3. Refraction
  4. Dispersion
Show answer

Answer: Refraction

Refraction is the bending of light when it passes from one transparent medium to another with different optical density (e.g., from air to glass).

Question 10medium

Which gas is produced during photosynthesis and released into the atmosphere?

  1. Carbon Dioxide
  2. Nitrogen
  3. Oxygen
  4. Methane
Show answer

Answer: Oxygen

Oxygen is released as a byproduct of photosynthesis when water molecules are split (photolysis) to provide electrons for the light reactions.

Question 11medium

The 'Law of Gravitation' was proposed by:

  1. Albert Einstein
  2. Galileo Galilei
  3. Isaac Newton
  4. Nicolaus Copernicus
Show answer

Answer: Isaac Newton

Sir Isaac Newton formulated the Universal Law of Gravitation (1687): F = Gm1m2/r², stating that every object attracts every other object with a force proportional to their masses and inversely proportional to the square of the distance between them.

Question 12hard

The 'Photoelectric Effect' was explained by:

  1. Isaac Newton
  2. Max Planck
  3. Albert Einstein
  4. Niels Bohr
Show answer

Answer: Albert Einstein

Albert Einstein explained the photoelectric effect in 1905 using the concept of light as photons (quanta of energy). This work won him the Nobel Prize in Physics (1921).

Question 13hard

Which is the lightest element in the periodic table?

  1. Helium
  2. Hydrogen
  3. Lithium
  4. Carbon
Show answer

Answer: Hydrogen

Hydrogen (H) is the lightest element with atomic number 1 and atomic mass ~1. It is also the most abundant element in the universe.

Question 14easy

Newton's First Law of Motion states that:

  1. A body at rest or uniform motion continues unless acted upon by an external force
  2. Force equals mass times acceleration
  3. Every action has an equal and opposite reaction
  4. Momentum is always conserved
Show answer

Answer: A body at rest or uniform motion continues unless acted upon by an external force

Newton's First Law (Law of Inertia): A body continues in its state of rest or of uniform motion in a straight line unless acted upon by an external unbalanced force. This is why we feel a jerk when a bus suddenly brakes.

Question 15easy

Newton's Second Law of Motion (F = ma) means:

  1. Force equals mass multiplied by acceleration
  2. Force is proportional to velocity
  3. Force is inversely proportional to mass
  4. All bodies accelerate at the same rate
Show answer

Answer: Force equals mass multiplied by acceleration

F = ma — the net force acting on a body equals the product of its mass and acceleration. A larger force produces greater acceleration; a larger mass requires more force to achieve the same acceleration.

Question 16easy

Newton's Third Law of Motion states:

  1. For every action there is an equal and opposite reaction
  2. Objects fall at 9.8 m/s²
  3. F = ma
  4. Momentum is conserved
Show answer

Answer: For every action there is an equal and opposite reaction

Newton's Third Law: For every action (force), there is an equal and opposite reaction. Example: rocket engines push exhaust gas backward (action), gas pushes rocket forward (reaction).

Question 17easy

The SI unit of force is:

  1. Newton (N)
  2. Dyne
  3. Joule
  4. Pascal
Show answer

Answer: Newton (N)

The SI unit of force is Newton (N). 1 N = 1 kg·m/s². 1 Newton is the force that gives a 1 kg mass an acceleration of 1 m/s². Named after Sir Isaac Newton.

Question 18easy

The acceleration due to gravity on Earth is approximately:

  1. 9.8 m/s²
  2. 9.8 m/s
  3. 10 m/s²
  4. 9 m/s²
Show answer

Answer: 9.8 m/s²

The acceleration due to gravity (g) on Earth's surface is approximately 9.8 m/s² (often approximated as 10 m/s²). It varies slightly with latitude (less at equator, more at poles) and altitude (decreases with height).

Question 19easy

Which law states that the total momentum of a closed system remains constant?

  1. Law of Conservation of Momentum
  2. Newton's Second Law
  3. Law of Conservation of Energy
  4. Archimedes' Principle
Show answer

Answer: Law of Conservation of Momentum

Law of Conservation of Momentum: The total linear momentum of a closed system (no external forces) remains constant. Total momentum before collision = Total momentum after collision.

Question 20easy

Archimedes' Principle states that:

  1. A body immersed in fluid experiences an upward buoyant force equal to the weight of displaced fluid
  2. Pressure increases with depth
  3. Fluids flow from high to low pressure
  4. All bodies sink in water
Show answer

Answer: A body immersed in fluid experiences an upward buoyant force equal to the weight of displaced fluid

Archimedes' Principle: When a body is fully or partially submerged in a fluid, it experiences a buoyant force equal to the weight of fluid displaced. This explains why ships float and hot air balloons rise.

Question 21easy

Work done is measured in:

  1. Joules (J)
  2. Watts (W)
  3. Newton (N)
  4. Pascal (Pa)
Show answer

Answer: Joules (J)

Work = Force × Distance. The SI unit of work is Joule (J). 1 J = 1 N × 1 m. Work is done only when a force displaces an object in the direction of the force.

Question 22easy

The speed of light in vacuum is:

  1. 3 × 10⁸ m/s (approximately 300,000 km/s)
  2. 3 × 10⁶ m/s
  3. 3 × 10¹⁰ m/s
  4. 3 × 10⁵ m/s
Show answer

Answer: 3 × 10⁸ m/s (approximately 300,000 km/s)

The speed of light in vacuum (c) is exactly 299,792,458 m/s ≈ 3 × 10⁸ m/s ≈ 300,000 km/s. Nothing can travel faster than the speed of light (Einstein's special relativity).

Question 23medium

Which phenomenon causes the rainbow to form?

  1. Dispersion and total internal reflection of sunlight in water droplets
  2. Reflection of sunlight only
  3. Refraction of light only
  4. Interference of light
Show answer

Answer: Dispersion and total internal reflection of sunlight in water droplets

Rainbow forms because sunlight entering a water droplet is refracted, internally reflected, and dispersed (separated into colours). The 7 colours (VIBGYOR — Violet, Indigo, Blue, Green, Yellow, Orange, Red) are separated.

Question 24medium

Total Internal Reflection occurs when:

  1. Light travels from denser to rarer medium at an angle greater than the critical angle
  2. Light hits a smooth surface
  3. Light passes through a prism
  4. Light bends around obstacles
Show answer

Answer: Light travels from denser to rarer medium at an angle greater than the critical angle

TIR occurs when light travels from a denser to a rarer medium and the angle of incidence exceeds the critical angle. TIR is the principle behind optical fibers and diamond's brilliance.

Question 25easy

A convex lens is used in:

  1. Cameras, magnifying glasses, and correcting farsightedness (hypermetropia)
  2. Correcting nearsightedness
  3. Rearview mirrors
  4. Periscopes
Show answer

Answer: Cameras, magnifying glasses, and correcting farsightedness (hypermetropia)

Convex (converging) lenses are thicker in the middle. They converge parallel light rays to a focal point. Used in cameras, magnifying glasses, telescopes (objective lens), and to correct farsightedness.

Question 26easy

A concave lens is used to correct:

  1. Myopia (nearsightedness/shortsightedness)
  2. Hypermetropia (farsightedness)
  3. Astigmatism
  4. Presbyopia
Show answer

Answer: Myopia (nearsightedness/shortsightedness)

Concave (diverging) lenses are thinner in the middle and diverge light rays. They are used to correct myopia (nearsightedness) — where distant objects appear blurry.

Question 27easy

Which colour of light has the shortest wavelength?

  1. Violet
  2. Red
  3. Yellow
  4. Blue
Show answer

Answer: Violet

Violet light has the shortest wavelength (~380-450 nm) and highest frequency in the visible spectrum. Red has the longest wavelength (~620-750 nm) and lowest frequency. The visible spectrum is VIBGYOR.

Question 28medium

The primary colours of light (additive colour mixing) are:

  1. Red, Green, Blue (RGB)
  2. Red, Yellow, Blue
  3. Red, Green, Yellow
  4. Cyan, Magenta, Yellow
Show answer

Answer: Red, Green, Blue (RGB)

Primary colours of light: Red, Green, Blue (RGB — additive mixing). Combining all three gives white light. Computer/TV screens use RGB. Pigment primary colours (subtractive) are Cyan, Magenta, Yellow (CMY).

Question 29easy

Sound travels fastest in:

  1. Solids (e.g., steel ~5,960 m/s)
  2. Liquids
  3. Gases
  4. Vacuum
Show answer

Answer: Solids (e.g., steel ~5,960 m/s)

Sound is a mechanical wave (needs a medium). It travels fastest in solids (5,960 m/s in steel), slower in liquids (1,497 m/s in water), and slowest in gases (343 m/s in air at 20°C). It cannot travel in vacuum.

Question 30easy

The speed of sound in air at 20°C is approximately:

  1. 343 m/s
  2. 300 m/s
  3. 1,497 m/s
  4. 1,000 m/s
Show answer

Answer: 343 m/s

Speed of sound in air at 20°C is about 343 m/s (approximately 1,235 km/h). Mach 1 = speed of sound. Aircraft flying faster than Mach 1 are supersonic.

Question 31easy

The human ear can hear sounds in the frequency range:

  1. 20 Hz to 20,000 Hz (20 kHz)
  2. 2 Hz to 200 Hz
  3. 200 Hz to 200,000 Hz
  4. 0-20 Hz
Show answer

Answer: 20 Hz to 20,000 Hz (20 kHz)

The human audible range is 20 Hz to 20,000 Hz. Sounds below 20 Hz are infrasound (heard by elephants and whales). Sounds above 20,000 Hz are ultrasound (heard by bats and dogs). Frequency is measured in Hertz (Hz).

Question 32easy

SONAR (Sound Navigation And Ranging) works on the principle of:

  1. Reflection of ultrasound waves
  2. Interference of sound waves
  3. Diffraction of sound
  4. Resonance of sound
Show answer

Answer: Reflection of ultrasound waves

SONAR uses ultrasound waves emitted into water; they reflect off objects (submarines, fish, seabed) and return to the source. By measuring the time taken, distance is calculated. Used in submarines and fish finding.

Question 33easy

The 'kitchen of the cell' (food factory) is:

  1. Chloroplast
  2. Mitochondria
  3. Ribosome
  4. Golgi apparatus
Show answer

Answer: Chloroplast

Chloroplasts are called the 'kitchen of the cell' because they carry out photosynthesis — using sunlight, CO₂, and water to produce glucose (food) and oxygen. Found only in plant cells. Contain chlorophyll.

Question 34easy

Nuclear fusion is the process of:

  1. Combining light nuclei (e.g., hydrogen isotopes) to form heavier nuclei, releasing energy
  2. Splitting heavy nuclei
  3. Beta decay
  4. Alpha emission
Show answer

Answer: Combining light nuclei (e.g., hydrogen isotopes) to form heavier nuclei, releasing energy

Nuclear fusion: light nuclei (H-2 deuterium + H-3 tritium) fuse at extremely high temperatures to form heavier nuclei (He-4), releasing enormous energy. Occurs in stars (the sun). Future clean energy source (ITER project).

Question 35easy

Einstein's famous equation E = mc² means:

  1. Energy equals mass times the speed of light squared — mass and energy are equivalent
  2. Energy = mass × charge
  3. E = momentum × velocity
  4. E = force × time
Show answer

Answer: Energy equals mass times the speed of light squared — mass and energy are equivalent

E = mc² (Einstein, 1905): energy (E) = mass (m) × speed of light squared (c²). This shows mass and energy are equivalent. Small mass converts to enormous energy (nuclear reactions). Basis for nuclear technology.

Question 36medium

Lasers work on the principle of:

  1. Stimulated emission of radiation — coherent, monochromatic, collimated light
  2. Spontaneous emission
  3. Fluorescence
  4. Bioluminescence
Show answer

Answer: Stimulated emission of radiation — coherent, monochromatic, collimated light

LASER (Light Amplification by Stimulated Emission of Radiation): photons stimulate excited atoms to emit identical photons — creating coherent (same phase), monochromatic (single wavelength), collimated (parallel) light. Used in medicine, cutting, communications.

Question 37easy

The green pigment in plants responsible for photosynthesis is:

  1. Chlorophyll
  2. Carotene
  3. Xanthophyll
  4. Anthocyanin
Show answer

Answer: Chlorophyll

Chlorophyll (mainly chlorophyll-a and chlorophyll-b) absorbs red and blue light for photosynthesis. Carotene (orange) and xanthophyll (yellow) are accessory pigments. Anthocyanin gives red/purple color to flowers/fruits.

Question 38easy

Birds belong to the class:

  1. Aves
  2. Mammalia
  3. Reptilia
  4. Amphibia
Show answer

Answer: Aves

Birds belong to Class Aves. They are warm-blooded vertebrates with feathers, beaks, hollow bones (for flight), and lay eggs with hard shells. About 10,000 species exist. Adapted for flight (wings, streamlined body).

Question 39medium

Adrenaline (epinephrine) is produced by:

  1. Adrenal medulla (inner part of adrenal gland)
  2. Pituitary gland
  3. Thyroid gland
  4. Pancreas
Show answer

Answer: Adrenal medulla (inner part of adrenal gland)

Adrenaline (epinephrine) is produced by the adrenal medulla (inner part of adrenal glands, above kidneys). It is the 'fight or flight' hormone — increases heart rate, blood pressure, and blood glucose during stress.

Question 40easy

The hormone responsible for 'fight or flight' response is:

  1. Adrenaline (epinephrine)
  2. Insulin
  3. Thyroxine
  4. Oxytocin
Show answer

Answer: Adrenaline (epinephrine)

Adrenaline (epinephrine) triggers the fight-or-flight response — dilates pupils, increases heart rate, raises blood pressure, diverts blood to muscles, releases glucose from glycogen stores.

Question 41medium

Which phenomenon explains why the sky is blue?

  1. Rayleigh scattering of sunlight by air molecules (shorter wavelengths scatter more)
  2. Reflection of ocean blue color
  3. Absorption by ozone
  4. Refraction of light
Show answer

Answer: Rayleigh scattering of sunlight by air molecules (shorter wavelengths scatter more)

Rayleigh scattering: air molecules scatter shorter wavelengths (blue/violet) much more than longer wavelengths (red). The sky appears blue because scattered blue light reaches our eyes from all directions. At sunset, light travels farther, and blue is scattered away, leaving red/orange.

Question 42medium

A mirage is caused by:

  1. Total internal reflection of light in hot air layers near the ground
  2. Reflection of sky off water
  3. Refraction by clouds
  4. Dispersion of light
Show answer

Answer: Total internal reflection of light in hot air layers near the ground

Mirage is caused by TIR — hot air near the ground is less dense (lower refractive index) than cooler air above. Light from the sky bends back upward as it tries to enter the low-density layer, creating an illusion of water (the sky reflection).

Question 43easy

The phenomenon of splitting of white light into its component colours is called:

  1. Dispersion
  2. Refraction
  3. Reflection
  4. Diffraction
Show answer

Answer: Dispersion

Dispersion: white light splits into its component colours (VIBGYOR) when it passes through a prism because different colours have different refractive indices. Violet refracts most; red least.

Question 44medium

Scattering of light by particles larger than wavelength of light is:

  1. Tyndall effect
  2. Rayleigh scattering
  3. Compton scattering
  4. Mie scattering
Show answer

Answer: Tyndall effect

Tyndall Effect: scattering of light by colloidal particles (particle size ~ wavelength of light). Makes a beam of light visible in a colloid (like dust in a sunbeam through a window). Named after John Tyndall.

Question 45medium

The principle of optical fiber is:

  1. Total Internal Reflection (TIR) of light through a glass/plastic fiber
  2. Refraction of light
  3. Absorption of light
  4. Interference of light
Show answer

Answer: Total Internal Reflection (TIR) of light through a glass/plastic fiber

Optical fibers work by TIR — light traveling through a dense glass core hits the glass-cladding interface at angles beyond the critical angle and is totally reflected, staying in the fiber over long distances. Used in communications.

Question 46easy

Which mirror is used in the rear-view mirror of vehicles?

  1. Convex mirror (gives a wider field of view)
  2. Concave mirror
  3. Plane mirror
  4. Parabolic mirror
Show answer

Answer: Convex mirror (gives a wider field of view)

Convex mirrors are used as rear-view/wing mirrors because they produce an erect, diminished virtual image with a wide field of view. Concave mirrors are used as shaving/makeup mirrors and in searchlights.

Question 47easy

Which mirror is used as a reflector in headlights and searchlights?

  1. Concave mirror (converges light into a parallel beam)
  2. Convex mirror
  3. Plane mirror
  4. Both concave and convex
Show answer

Answer: Concave mirror (converges light into a parallel beam)

Concave (converging) mirrors are used in headlights, searchlights, solar concentrators, and telescopes. When a light source is placed at the focal point, the reflected rays form a parallel (collimated) beam.

Question 48medium

The refractive index of a medium is the ratio of:

  1. Speed of light in vacuum to speed of light in that medium (n = c/v)
  2. Wavelength in vacuum to wavelength in medium
  3. Frequency in medium to frequency in vacuum
  4. Density of medium to density of vacuum
Show answer

Answer: Speed of light in vacuum to speed of light in that medium (n = c/v)

Refractive index (n) = c/v (speed of light in vacuum / speed in medium). Higher n = slower light, more bending. Glass n ≈ 1.5, Water n ≈ 1.33, Diamond n ≈ 2.42 (hence diamond's high reflectance).

Question 49easy

The household electricity supply in India is:

  1. 230 V AC at 50 Hz
  2. 110 V AC at 60 Hz
  3. 220 V DC
  4. 415 V AC at 50 Hz
Show answer

Answer: 230 V AC at 50 Hz

India uses 230 V AC at 50 Hz for household supply. USA uses 110-120 V at 60 Hz. Three-phase supply for industries is 415 V. The frequency (50 Hz) means current changes direction 50 times per second.

Question 50easy

The unit of electrical energy consumed is:

  1. Kilowatt-hour (kWh) — also called a 'unit'
  2. Joule only
  3. Watt
  4. Volt
Show answer

Answer: Kilowatt-hour (kWh) — also called a 'unit'

Electrical energy consumed = Power (kW) × Time (hours). 1 kWh = 1 'unit' of electricity on the electricity bill. 1 kWh = 3.6 × 10⁶ Joules. A 1000 W (1 kW) appliance running for 1 hour uses 1 unit.

Question 51easy

The noble gases (Group 18) are unreactive because:

  1. They have completely filled outermost electron shells (8 electrons — stable octet)
  2. They are radioactive
  3. They have no protons
  4. They are liquids at room temperature
Show answer

Answer: They have completely filled outermost electron shells (8 electrons — stable octet)

Noble gases (He, Ne, Ar, Kr, Xe, Rn) have completely filled outermost electron shells (He=2, others=8), making them extremely stable and unreactive. They are called 'inert gases'. Used in lighting (neon, argon).

Question 52easy

X-rays were discovered by:

  1. Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen (1895)
  2. Marie Curie
  3. Ernest Rutherford
  4. Henri Becquerel
Show answer

Answer: Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen (1895)

X-rays were discovered by Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen on 8 November 1895. He won the first Nobel Prize in Physics (1901) for this discovery. X-rays penetrate soft tissue but are absorbed by dense materials like bone.

Question 53easy

Ultrasound imaging uses:

  1. High-frequency sound waves (>20,000 Hz) to image internal organs
  2. X-rays
  3. Magnetic fields
  4. Radioactive tracers
Show answer

Answer: High-frequency sound waves (>20,000 Hz) to image internal organs

Ultrasound imaging (sonography) uses high-frequency sound waves. A transducer sends sound waves into the body; echoes returning from organs are converted into images. Safe (no radiation) — used for fetal imaging, abdominal organs.

Question 54easy

The nearest star to Earth (after the Sun) is:

  1. Proxima Centauri (4.24 light years away)
  2. Alpha Centauri A
  3. Sirius
  4. Barnard's Star
Show answer

Answer: Proxima Centauri (4.24 light years away)

Proxima Centauri is the nearest star to Earth at 4.24 light years (about 40 trillion km). It is part of the Alpha Centauri triple star system. It has at least one exoplanet (Proxima b) in the habitable zone.

Question 55easy

A 'light year' is:

  1. The distance light travels in one year (about 9.46 × 10¹² km)
  2. The time for light to reach the Moon
  3. The brightness of a star
  4. The age of the universe in years
Show answer

Answer: The distance light travels in one year (about 9.46 × 10¹² km)

A light year is the distance light travels in one year: approximately 9.46 trillion km (9.46 × 10¹² km). It is a unit of distance, not time. Light from the Sun takes about 8 minutes to reach Earth.

Question 56medium

The Big Bang theory states that the universe began:

  1. About 13.8 billion years ago from an extremely hot, dense state that rapidly expanded
  2. 5 billion years ago
  3. Always existed (steady state)
  4. Was created by a star explosion
Show answer

Answer: About 13.8 billion years ago from an extremely hot, dense state that rapidly expanded

Big Bang Theory: the universe began about 13.8 billion years ago from an extremely hot, dense singularity that rapidly expanded (Big Bang). Evidence: cosmic microwave background radiation (CMB), redshift of galaxies, abundance of light elements.

Question 57medium

Black holes are formed when:

  1. Massive stars collapse after exhausting their nuclear fuel (core collapse → extreme gravity from which light cannot escape)
  2. Stars explode
  3. Two galaxies merge
  4. Planets are destroyed
Show answer

Answer: Massive stars collapse after exhausting their nuclear fuel (core collapse → extreme gravity from which light cannot escape)

Black holes form when massive stars (>20 solar masses) exhaust nuclear fuel and their cores collapse under gravity. The gravity is so strong that even light cannot escape (escape velocity > c). Detected through gravitational effects.

Question 58medium

The correct order of electromagnetic spectrum from lowest to highest frequency is:

  1. Radio waves → Microwaves → IR → Visible → UV → X-rays → Gamma rays
  2. Gamma → X-ray → UV → Visible → IR → Microwave → Radio
  3. X-ray → UV → Visible → IR → Radio
  4. Radio → Visible → UV → X-ray
Show answer

Answer: Radio waves → Microwaves → IR → Visible → UV → X-rays → Gamma rays

Electromagnetic spectrum by increasing frequency (and energy): Radio < Microwaves < Infrared < Visible light < Ultraviolet < X-rays < Gamma rays. All travel at speed of light (3×10⁸ m/s) in vacuum.

Question 59easy

Which gas is produced when acids react with active metals (like Zn, Fe, Mg)?

  1. Hydrogen gas (H₂) — Zn + H₂SO₄ → ZnSO₄ + H₂↑
  2. Oxygen gas
  3. Carbon dioxide
  4. Nitrogen gas
Show answer

Answer: Hydrogen gas (H₂) — Zn + H₂SO₄ → ZnSO₄ + H₂↑

When active metals react with dilute acids, hydrogen gas is produced: Zn + H₂SO₄ → ZnSO₄ + H₂↑. This can be tested by holding a burning splint near the gas — it burns with a squeaky pop sound.

Question 60medium

The autonomic nervous system controls:

  1. Involuntary functions like heartbeat, digestion, breathing, and glandular secretions
  2. Voluntary movements
  3. Speech and language
  4. Higher thinking
Show answer

Answer: Involuntary functions like heartbeat, digestion, breathing, and glandular secretions

The autonomic nervous system (ANS) controls involuntary body functions: heart rate, blood pressure, digestion, glandular activity, and respiration. It has two divisions: sympathetic (fight-or-flight) and parasympathetic (rest-and-digest).

Question 61easy

The pressure at which blood is pumped out of the heart is called:

  1. Blood pressure — systolic (contraction) over diastolic (relaxation), normal 120/80 mmHg
  2. Pulse rate
  3. Cardiac output
  4. Heart rate
Show answer

Answer: Blood pressure — systolic (contraction) over diastolic (relaxation), normal 120/80 mmHg

Blood pressure is the force exerted by blood on artery walls. Systolic pressure (top number) = when heart contracts (~120 mmHg). Diastolic pressure (bottom number) = when heart relaxes (~80 mmHg). High BP (hypertension) > 140/90 mmHg.

Question 62easy

The process by which plants lose water through their leaves is:

  1. Transpiration — primarily through stomata; drives the ascent of xylem sap
  2. Photosynthesis
  3. Respiration
  4. Translocation
Show answer

Answer: Transpiration — primarily through stomata; drives the ascent of xylem sap

Transpiration is the evaporation of water from plant leaves (mainly through stomata). It creates a tension (negative pressure) in the xylem, pulling water upward from roots. Factors affecting transpiration: temperature, humidity, wind, light.

Question 63medium

Pollination by wind is called:

  1. Anemophily — pollen grains are light and produced in large quantities (e.g., grasses, corn)
  2. Entomophily (insects)
  3. Ornithophily (birds)
  4. Hydrophily (water)
Show answer

Answer: Anemophily — pollen grains are light and produced in large quantities (e.g., grasses, corn)

Anemophily (wind pollination): pollen is lightweight, small, smooth, and produced abundantly. Examples: grasses, wheat, maize, oak. Entomophily (insect pollination): pollen is sticky, fragrant flowers. Zoophily includes bird (ornithophily) and bat pollination.

Question 64medium

A lactometer is used to measure:

  1. The purity/density of milk (to detect adulteration with water)
  2. Temperature of milk
  3. Acidity of milk
  4. Fat content directly
Show answer

Answer: The purity/density of milk (to detect adulteration with water)

A lactometer measures the density (specific gravity) of milk. Pure milk has specific gravity ~1.028-1.033. When water is added, density decreases. It is based on Archimedes' principle — the lactometer floats at different levels depending on milk density.

Question 65medium

A body in uniform circular motion has:

  1. Constant speed but changing velocity (centripetal acceleration directed toward center)
  2. Constant velocity
  3. Zero acceleration
  4. Increasing speed
Show answer

Answer: Constant speed but changing velocity (centripetal acceleration directed toward center)

In uniform circular motion, speed (magnitude of velocity) is constant but velocity direction continuously changes. This requires centripetal acceleration = v²/r directed toward the center. The centripetal force provides this acceleration (tension, gravity, friction, etc.).

Question 66medium

Newton's Law of Gravitation states that gravitational force is:

  1. Directly proportional to product of masses and inversely proportional to square of distance (F = Gm₁m₂/r²)
  2. Equal to mass times acceleration
  3. Directly proportional to distance
  4. Inversely proportional to mass
Show answer

Answer: Directly proportional to product of masses and inversely proportional to square of distance (F = Gm₁m₂/r²)

Newton's Universal Law of Gravitation: F = Gm₁m₂/r², where G = 6.674×10⁻¹¹ N·m²/kg² is the gravitational constant. The force is attractive, acts between all masses, and decreases with square of distance.

Question 67medium

When a ball is thrown upward, at the highest point:

  1. Velocity = 0 but acceleration = g (9.8 m/s²) downward (still under gravity)
  2. Both velocity and acceleration = 0
  3. Only acceleration = 0
  4. Velocity is maximum
Show answer

Answer: Velocity = 0 but acceleration = g (9.8 m/s²) downward (still under gravity)

At the highest point of projectile motion, the vertical velocity component = 0 (ball momentarily stops going up). However, gravitational acceleration (g = 9.8 m/s² downward) acts at all times — it is g that decelerates the ball going up and accelerates it coming down.

Question 68medium

Nuclear energy in power plants is generated by:

  1. Controlled nuclear fission of U-235 or Pu-239 in reactors (chain reaction releases heat to produce steam)
  2. Nuclear fusion
  3. Radioactive decay heat only
  4. Chemical combustion
Show answer

Answer: Controlled nuclear fission of U-235 or Pu-239 in reactors (chain reaction releases heat to produce steam)

Nuclear power plants use controlled fission: neutrons split U-235 (or Pu-239) atoms, releasing energy and 2-3 more neutrons (chain reaction). Heat is used to boil water → steam → turbine → electricity. India's reactors: Tarapur, Kalpakkam, Kaiga, Kudankulam, etc.

Question 69easy

An ionic bond is formed by:

  1. Transfer of electrons from a metal (loses electrons, becomes cation) to a non-metal (gains electrons, becomes anion)
  2. Sharing of electrons
  3. Sharing of protons
  4. Attraction between same charges
Show answer

Answer: Transfer of electrons from a metal (loses electrons, becomes cation) to a non-metal (gains electrons, becomes anion)

Ionic bonds form when electronegativity difference is large (>1.7): metal loses electron(s) → cation; non-metal gains electron(s) → anion. Oppositely charged ions attract. Examples: NaCl, MgO, CaCl₂. Ionic compounds have high melting points, conduct electricity when dissolved.

Question 70medium

The focal length of a concave mirror is:

  1. Negative (by sign convention) — half of the radius of curvature (f = R/2), and concave mirrors can form real or virtual images
  2. Positive always
  3. Equal to radius of curvature
  4. Zero
Show answer

Answer: Negative (by sign convention) — half of the radius of curvature (f = R/2), and concave mirrors can form real or virtual images

For a concave mirror (converging): focal length f = R/2 (R = radius of curvature). By the New Cartesian sign convention, f is negative for concave mirrors. Uses: headlights, solar furnaces, dental/ENT mirrors, reflecting telescopes (real image for object beyond f).

Question 71medium

Optical fiber communication works on the principle of:

  1. Total Internal Reflection (TIR) — light trapped inside the fiber travels long distances with minimal loss
  2. Refraction
  3. Reflection at a glass-air interface below critical angle
  4. Diffraction
Show answer

Answer: Total Internal Reflection (TIR) — light trapped inside the fiber travels long distances with minimal loss

Optical fibers use TIR: light enters the dense glass core and hits the core-cladding boundary at angles greater than the critical angle, reflecting completely back into the core. Light travels zigzag inside the fiber from source to destination with very low signal loss.

Question 72medium

The Doppler Effect in sound refers to:

  1. Change in apparent frequency of sound when source and observer are in relative motion (higher freq when approaching, lower when receding)
  2. Reflection of sound
  3. Speed change of sound
  4. Loudness change
Show answer

Answer: Change in apparent frequency of sound when source and observer are in relative motion (higher freq when approaching, lower when receding)

Doppler Effect: when a source moves toward the observer, sound waves compress → higher frequency (higher pitch). When moving away → lower frequency. Application: radar speed guns, ultrasound (fetal heartbeat), astronomical red-shift/blue-shift of light.

Question 73hard

An echo is produced when sound is reflected by a surface that is at least:

  1. 17 meters away (sound takes at least 0.1 s to return — minimum delay for human ear to distinguish echo from original sound)
  2. 1 meter away
  3. 5 meters away
  4. 100 meters away
Show answer

Answer: 17 meters away (sound takes at least 0.1 s to return — minimum delay for human ear to distinguish echo from original sound)

For an echo to be heard distinctly, the reflected sound must return at least 0.1 second after the original. Since sound travels at ~340 m/s, total distance = 340 × 0.1 = 34 m. So the reflecting surface must be at least 34/2 = 17 m away.

Question 74medium

Ultrasound is used in medical sonography because:

  1. High-frequency sound (>20,000 Hz) reflects differently at tissue boundaries, creating images without radiation (safe for fetal imaging)
  2. It is audible
  3. It passes through all tissues without reflection
  4. It uses X-ray radiation
Show answer

Answer: High-frequency sound (>20,000 Hz) reflects differently at tissue boundaries, creating images without radiation (safe for fetal imaging)

Ultrasound (1-20 MHz for medical use) reflects at interfaces between different tissue densities. Transducer emits pulses and detects echoes; computer reconstructs images. Safe (no ionizing radiation), used for fetal imaging, organ scanning, and detecting kidney stones.

Question 75medium

Stars generate energy through:

  1. Nuclear fusion — hydrogen atoms fuse to form helium in the core, releasing energy (E=mc²) — same process as hydrogen bomb
  2. Nuclear fission
  3. Chemical combustion
  4. Gravitational collapse
Show answer

Answer: Nuclear fusion — hydrogen atoms fuse to form helium in the core, releasing energy (E=mc²) — same process as hydrogen bomb

Stars like the Sun fuse hydrogen (H) to helium (He) in their cores: 4 ¹H → ⁴He + energy. The slight mass decrease (mass defect) converts to energy via E=mc². The Sun converts ~600 million tons of H to He every second, releasing energy as light and heat.

Question 76medium

LED (Light Emitting Diode) produces light through:

  1. Electroluminescence — electrons recombining with holes in a semiconductor p-n junction release energy as photons
  2. Incandescence (heating of filament)
  3. Fluorescence (UV exciting phosphors)
  4. Plasma discharge
Show answer

Answer: Electroluminescence — electrons recombining with holes in a semiconductor p-n junction release energy as photons

LED: when forward-biased, electrons from n-type and holes from p-type recombine at the junction, releasing energy as photons. Color depends on semiconductor material (bandgap): GaAs (infrared), GaN (blue/white), GaP (green/red). LEDs use 80-90% less energy than incandescent bulbs.

Question 77easy

A pulley is used to:

  1. Change the direction of force and/or reduce the effort needed to lift a load (mechanical advantage)
  2. Increase speed only
  3. Store energy
  4. Convert heat to work
Show answer

Answer: Change the direction of force and/or reduce the effort needed to lift a load (mechanical advantage)

A single fixed pulley changes the direction of force (effort direction changes, but magnitude stays same — no mechanical advantage). A movable pulley halves the effort needed (MA=2). Combination block-and-tackle systems provide higher mechanical advantages for cranes and elevators.

Question 78easy

The rate at which electrical energy is consumed is called:

  1. Power (P = VI = I²R = V²/R), measured in Watts — 1 Watt = 1 Joule per second
  2. Energy
  3. Resistance
  4. Current
Show answer

Answer: Power (P = VI = I²R = V²/R), measured in Watts — 1 Watt = 1 Joule per second

Electrical power P = VI (Voltage × Current) = I²R = V²/R. Unit: Watt (W) or kilowatt (kW). Electrical energy consumed = P × t. 1 unit (kWh) = 1000 W × 1 hour = 3.6×10⁶ J. Electricity bills are based on units consumed.

Question 79medium

The speed of sound in air at 0°C is approximately:

  1. 331 m/s (increases by 0.6 m/s per °C rise — at 25°C ≈ 346 m/s)
  2. 3×10⁸ m/s
  3. 1500 m/s
  4. 100 m/s
Show answer

Answer: 331 m/s (increases by 0.6 m/s per °C rise — at 25°C ≈ 346 m/s)

Speed of sound in dry air at 0°C ≈ 331 m/s; at 25°C ≈ 346 m/s. Speed increases with temperature and humidity. Speed in water ≈ 1480 m/s; in steel ≈ 5100 m/s. Sound is fastest in solids because molecules are more tightly packed.

Question 80easy

The loudness of sound is measured in:

  1. Decibels (dB) — a logarithmic scale; 0 dB = threshold of hearing; 120 dB = pain threshold; normal conversation ≈ 60 dB
  2. Hertz
  3. Watts
  4. Metres per second
Show answer

Answer: Decibels (dB) — a logarithmic scale; 0 dB = threshold of hearing; 120 dB = pain threshold; normal conversation ≈ 60 dB

Decibel (dB) scale: 0 dB (threshold of hearing), 30 dB (whisper), 60 dB (normal conversation), 85 dB (hearing damage starts with prolonged exposure), 120 dB (pain threshold), 140+ dB (immediate damage). Frequency (pitch) is measured in Hertz (Hz).

Question 81easy

Photosynthesis occurs in which part of the plant cell?

  1. Chloroplast — specifically in the thylakoid membranes (light reactions) and stroma (dark reactions/Calvin cycle)
  2. Mitochondria
  3. Nucleus
  4. Cell wall
Show answer

Answer: Chloroplast — specifically in the thylakoid membranes (light reactions) and stroma (dark reactions/Calvin cycle)

Chloroplasts contain chlorophyll and are the sites of photosynthesis. Light reactions occur in the thylakoid membranes (stacks of grana) — capture light energy, produce ATP and NADPH, release O₂. Calvin cycle (dark reactions) occurs in the stroma — fixes CO₂ into glucose.

Question 82easy

The theory of relativity (Special and General) was developed by:

  1. Albert Einstein — Special Relativity (1905, E=mc²) and General Relativity (1915, gravity as curvature of spacetime)
  2. Isaac Newton
  3. Max Planck
  4. Niels Bohr
Show answer

Answer: Albert Einstein — Special Relativity (1905, E=mc²) and General Relativity (1915, gravity as curvature of spacetime)

Einstein: Special Relativity (1905) — at high speeds, time dilates, length contracts, mass increases; E=mc² (mass-energy equivalence). General Relativity (1915) — gravity is curvature of spacetime by mass/energy. Predicted: gravitational waves, black holes, gravitational lensing.

Question 83medium

Artificial Intelligence (AI) is primarily based on:

  1. Machine learning — algorithms that improve with data; deep learning uses neural networks mimicking the brain
  2. Physical robots only
  3. Simple rule-based programs only
  4. Quantum computers only
Show answer

Answer: Machine learning — algorithms that improve with data; deep learning uses neural networks mimicking the brain

Modern AI: Machine Learning (ML) — algorithms learn patterns from data. Deep Learning (DL): multi-layer artificial neural networks (ANNs) — basis for image recognition, language models (GPT), voice assistants. Natural Language Processing (NLP), Computer Vision, and Reinforcement Learning are sub-fields.

Question 84easy

The process by which green plants prepare food using sunlight is called photosynthesis. Which gas is released as a byproduct?

  1. Oxygen (O₂) — released from splitting of water molecules (photolysis) during light reactions
  2. Carbon dioxide
  3. Nitrogen
  4. Hydrogen
Show answer

Answer: Oxygen (O₂) — released from splitting of water molecules (photolysis) during light reactions

6CO₂ + 6H₂O + light energy → C₆H₁₂O₆ + 6O₂. O₂ is released from water molecules split during light reactions (photolysis of water). This O₂ is the source of almost all atmospheric oxygen. CO₂ is fixed into glucose in the Calvin cycle (dark reactions).

Question 85easy

The human eye can see objects clearly because:

  1. The eye lens focuses light on the retina — ciliary muscles change lens shape (accommodation) for near and far vision
  2. The cornea stores images
  3. The iris captures light
  4. Optic nerve detects light directly
Show answer

Answer: The eye lens focuses light on the retina — ciliary muscles change lens shape (accommodation) for near and far vision

The eye works like a camera: light enters through cornea (main refracting surface), passes through iris (controls light amount) and lens (fine-focuses by changing shape — accommodation), and forms an inverted image on the retina. Rods (dim light, black/white) and cones (color, bright light) in retina convert light to nerve signals.

Question 86medium

The pH of blood is maintained in the range:

  1. 7.35–7.45 (slightly alkaline) — deviation causes acidosis (<7.35) or alkalosis (>7.45), both life-threatening
  2. 6.8–7.0
  3. 7.0 exactly
  4. 8.0–8.5
Show answer

Answer: 7.35–7.45 (slightly alkaline) — deviation causes acidosis (<7.35) or alkalosis (>7.45), both life-threatening

Blood pH is tightly regulated between 7.35-7.45 (slightly alkaline). Buffer systems: bicarbonate buffer (HCO₃⁻/H₂CO₃), protein buffer (hemoglobin), and phosphate buffer. Acidosis (pH < 7.35): excess CO₂ or metabolic acid. Alkalosis (pH > 7.45): excess base. Outside 6.8-7.8 is fatal.

Question 87easy

The branch of science dealing with the study of stars and celestial bodies is:

  1. Astronomy — whereas astrology (predicting events from star positions) is not a science
  2. Geology
  3. Meteorology (weather)
  4. Oceanography
Show answer

Answer: Astronomy — whereas astrology (predicting events from star positions) is not a science

Astronomy: scientific study of celestial objects (stars, planets, galaxies, black holes), space, and the universe. Astrophysics: applies physics to understand how celestial objects work. Cosmology: study of the universe's origin, evolution, and structure. Meteorology: study of Earth's atmosphere/weather.

Question 88easy

Which part of the eye controls the amount of light entering?

  1. Iris (the colored part) — circular and radial muscles change pupil size: dilates in dim light (parasympathetic), constricts in bright light (sympathetic)
  2. Cornea
  3. Lens
  4. Retina
Show answer

Answer: Iris (the colored part) — circular and radial muscles change pupil size: dilates in dim light (parasympathetic), constricts in bright light (sympathetic)

Iris: colored part of the eye (contains pigment melanin — more melanin = darker iris). Circular muscles (parasympathetic): contract → pupil dilates (dim light). Radial muscles (sympathetic): contract → pupil constricts (bright light). Pupil is the hole through which light enters.

Question 89medium

The chemical used in photography (traditional silver-based film) is:

  1. Silver bromide (AgBr) or silver chloride (AgCl) — light-sensitive, reduces to black silver when exposed to light
  2. Silver nitrate only
  3. Gold chloride
  4. Platinum salts
Show answer

Answer: Silver bromide (AgBr) or silver chloride (AgCl) — light-sensitive, reduces to black silver when exposed to light

Traditional photographic film: silver halides (AgBr, AgCl) coated on film. When light hits AgBr, Ag⁺ is reduced to Ag (black) — forming a latent image. Developer (chemical reductor) amplifies this; fixer (sodium thiosulfate) removes unexposed AgBr. Digital cameras replaced film with CCD/CMOS sensors.

Question 90medium

The phenomenon of 'capillary action' is due to:

  1. Adhesion (water attracted to glass/plant cell walls) and cohesion (water-water attraction via H bonds) — water rises in narrow tubes against gravity
  2. Gravity alone
  3. Atmospheric pressure alone
  4. Osmosis
Show answer

Answer: Adhesion (water attracted to glass/plant cell walls) and cohesion (water-water attraction via H bonds) — water rises in narrow tubes against gravity

Capillary action: water rises in narrow tubes (capillaries) against gravity. Due to: adhesion (water attracted to tube walls) > gravity on that water column + cohesion (water molecules attract each other). Occurs in plant xylem vessels (helps water ascent), paper (chromatography), and wicks (candles, lamps).

Question 91easy

Phototropism in plants means:

  1. Growth of plant parts in response to light — shoots grow toward light (positive phototropism); roots grow away from light (negative phototropism)
  2. Response to gravity
  3. Response to touch
  4. Response to water
Show answer

Answer: Growth of plant parts in response to light — shoots grow toward light (positive phototropism); roots grow away from light (negative phototropism)

Tropism: directed growth response to a stimulus. Phototropism: light. Geotropism (gravitropism): gravity (roots down, shoots up). Hydrotropism: water (roots toward water). Thigmotropism: touch (tendrils wrap around supports). Chemotropism: chemicals (pollen tube grows toward ovule). Controlled by auxin redistribution.

Question 92medium

Peristalsis is the movement that:

  1. Propels food through the digestive tract — wave-like contraction and relaxation of smooth muscles in esophagus, stomach, and intestines
  2. Pumps blood through the heart
  3. Moves air through lungs
  4. Transports urine through ureters
Show answer

Answer: Propels food through the digestive tract — wave-like contraction and relaxation of smooth muscles in esophagus, stomach, and intestines

Peristalsis: wave-like contractions of circular and longitudinal smooth muscles in the digestive tract. Circular muscles contract behind a food bolus; longitudinal muscles relax → bolus moves forward. Occurs in esophagus (pushes food to stomach even against gravity), stomach (churning), small/large intestines. Also in ureters (urine to bladder).

Question 93medium

The phenomenon of 'surface tension' in water explains:

  1. Why water strider insects can walk on water, why water forms droplets, and why a needle can float on still water surface
  2. Why water conducts electricity
  3. Why water is transparent
  4. Why water has high boiling point
Show answer

Answer: Why water strider insects can walk on water, why water forms droplets, and why a needle can float on still water surface

Surface tension: cohesive forces between water molecules at the surface create a 'skin' that resists deformation. Surface molecules have fewer neighbors → net inward pull. Water has high surface tension (72.8 mN/m at 25°C) due to H-bonding. Soap lowers surface tension → bubbles, better wetting.

Question 94easy

The study of the human mind and behavior is:

  1. Psychology (psyche = mind/soul; logos = study) — scientific study of mental processes and behavior
  2. Psychiatry (medical treatment of mental disorders)
  3. Sociology (study of society)
  4. Neuroscience (study of nervous system)
Show answer

Answer: Psychology (psyche = mind/soul; logos = study) — scientific study of mental processes and behavior

Psychology: scientific study of behavior and mental processes (perception, cognition, emotion, personality, behavior). Wilhelm Wundt (1879) opened first experimental psychology lab (Leipzig). Major approaches: Freudian/psychoanalytic, behavioral, cognitive, humanistic, and biological. Psychiatry: medical specialty treating mental disorders (uses medications).

Question 95easy

Photosynthesis equation is:

  1. 6CO₂ + 6H₂O + light energy → C₆H₁₂O₆ + 6O₂
  2. C₆H₁₂O₆ + 6O₂ → 6CO₂ + 6H₂O + energy
  3. CO₂ + H₂O → CH₄ + O₂
  4. 6CO₂ + 12H₂O → C₆H₁₂O₆ + 6H₂O + 6O₂
Show answer

Answer: 6CO₂ + 6H₂O + light energy → C₆H₁₂O₆ + 6O₂

Photosynthesis: 6CO₂ + 6H₂O + light energy → C₆H₁₂O₆ + 6O₂. Plants use sunlight (chlorophyll) to convert CO₂ and water into glucose (food) and oxygen. Oxygen is the by-product — vital for life on Earth.

Question 96easy

Vitamin D deficiency causes:

  1. Rickets (in children) and Osteomalacia (in adults)
  2. Scurvy
  3. Night blindness
  4. Beriberi
Show answer

Answer: Rickets (in children) and Osteomalacia (in adults)

Vitamin D deficiency causes Rickets (soft/weak bones in children — bowed legs) and Osteomalacia (soft bones in adults). Vitamin D is synthesized by skin in sunlight. Sources: fish liver oil, eggs, fortified milk.

Question 97easy

Night blindness is caused by deficiency of:

  1. Vitamin A (retinol)
  2. Vitamin C
  3. Vitamin D
  4. Vitamin B12
Show answer

Answer: Vitamin A (retinol)

Vitamin A deficiency causes night blindness (inability to see in dim light) and xerophthalmia (dry eyes). Vitamin A is needed for rhodopsin production in rod cells of retina. Sources: carrots, green leafy vegetables, fish liver.

Question 98medium

The pH of human blood is approximately:

  1. 7.35-7.45 (slightly alkaline)
  2. 7.0 (neutral)
  3. 6.5 (acidic)
  4. 8.0 (alkaline)
Show answer

Answer: 7.35-7.45 (slightly alkaline)

Human blood pH is tightly regulated between 7.35-7.45 (slightly alkaline). Acidosis (pH < 7.35) and alkalosis (pH > 7.45) are life-threatening conditions. The body uses buffers (bicarbonate, phosphate) to maintain blood pH.

Question 99easy

C.V. Raman won the Nobel Prize in Physics (1930) for:

  1. Discovery of Raman Effect (inelastic scattering of photons by molecules)
  2. Discovery of radioactivity
  3. Discovery of X-rays
  4. Theory of relativity
Show answer

Answer: Discovery of Raman Effect (inelastic scattering of photons by molecules)

C.V. Raman (Chandrasekhara Venkata Raman) discovered the Raman Effect in 1928 — when light scatters from molecules, a small fraction changes wavelength due to energy exchange with molecular vibrations. He won Nobel Prize in 1930 — first Asian scientist to win it.

Question 100medium

Which instrument is used to measure the wavelength of light?

  1. Spectrometer (spectroscope)
  2. Barometer
  3. Hygrometer
  4. Galvanometer
Show answer

Answer: Spectrometer (spectroscope)

A spectrometer (or spectroscope) disperses light into its component wavelengths (spectrum). Used to identify elements (each has unique spectral lines — like a fingerprint) and measure wavelengths. Basis of spectroscopy.

Question 101medium

The Raman Effect (for which C.V. Raman won Nobel Prize in Physics 1930) involves:

  1. Inelastic scattering of light by molecules — scattered light has different wavelength from incident light
  2. Elastic scattering of light
  3. Total internal reflection
  4. Photoelectric effect
Show answer

Answer: Inelastic scattering of light by molecules — scattered light has different wavelength from incident light

Raman Effect (1928): when monochromatic light passes through a transparent medium, some scattered light has different wavelengths (Raman scattering — inelastic). This reveals molecular composition. C.V. Raman won Nobel Prize 1930 — first Asian Nobel laureate in sciences.

Question 102medium

DRDO (Defence Research and Development Organisation) is associated with:

  1. Defence technology R&D — missiles (Agni, Prithvi), radar, armaments, Tejas fighter aircraft
  2. Space research
  3. Agricultural research
  4. Medical research
Show answer

Answer: Defence technology R&D — missiles (Agni, Prithvi), radar, armaments, Tejas fighter aircraft

DRDO (est. 1958, HQ: New Delhi) is India's defence R&D agency. Key achievements: Agni and Prithvi ballistic missiles, BrahMos supersonic cruise missile (India-Russia JV), Tejas light combat aircraft, Arjun tank, and electronic warfare systems.

Question 103medium

Pascal's Law states that:

  1. Pressure applied to an enclosed fluid is transmitted equally in all directions (basis of hydraulic systems)
  2. Pressure increases with velocity in flowing fluids
  3. Buoyant force equals weight of displaced fluid
  4. Gases expand to fill their container
Show answer

Answer: Pressure applied to an enclosed fluid is transmitted equally in all directions (basis of hydraulic systems)

Pascal's Law: pressure applied to an enclosed fluid is transmitted equally and without change throughout the fluid (in all directions). Applications: hydraulic press, hydraulic brakes, hydraulic jacks, dentist's chairs. A small force can lift huge weights.

Question 104medium

The principle behind an aircraft wing generating lift is:

  1. Bernoulli's Principle — air moves faster over curved upper surface, creating lower pressure on top than below, generating lift
  2. Newton's 3rd Law alone
  3. Gravity reversal
  4. Magnetic levitation
Show answer

Answer: Bernoulli's Principle — air moves faster over curved upper surface, creating lower pressure on top than below, generating lift

Aircraft wings (airfoils) use Bernoulli's Principle: air over the curved upper surface travels faster than air below, creating lower pressure above the wing. The pressure difference generates an upward lift force. Newton's 3rd Law also contributes (wing deflects air downward).

Question 105medium

The phenomenon responsible for the blue color of the sky is:

  1. Rayleigh Scattering — shorter wavelengths (blue, violet) scatter more by atmospheric molecules
  2. Refraction
  3. Reflection
  4. Diffraction
Show answer

Answer: Rayleigh Scattering — shorter wavelengths (blue, violet) scatter more by atmospheric molecules

Rayleigh Scattering: atmospheric molecules (N₂, O₂) scatter shorter wavelengths (blue, violet) more than longer wavelengths (red, orange). Blue is scattered in all directions, making the sky appear blue. At sunrise/sunset, light travels through more atmosphere → sky appears red/orange.

Question 106easy

Which vitamin is synthesized by the human body when exposed to sunlight?

  1. Vitamin D (cholecalciferol) — UV-B rays convert 7-dehydrocholesterol in skin to Vitamin D3
  2. Vitamin C
  3. Vitamin B12
  4. Vitamin A
Show answer

Answer: Vitamin D (cholecalciferol) — UV-B rays convert 7-dehydrocholesterol in skin to Vitamin D3

UV-B radiation from sunlight converts 7-dehydrocholesterol (in skin) to Vitamin D3 (cholecalciferol). It is then processed in liver and kidneys. Vitamin D is essential for calcium absorption, bone health, and immune function. Deficiency causes rickets (children), osteomalacia (adults).

Question 107medium

The function of auxin (IAA) in plants is:

  1. Promote cell elongation in stems (phototropism — shoot bends toward light because auxin redistributes to shaded side)
  2. Promote fruit ripening
  3. Inhibit seed germination
  4. Kill insects
Show answer

Answer: Promote cell elongation in stems (phototropism — shoot bends toward light because auxin redistributes to shaded side)

Auxin (Indole-3-acetic acid, IAA) is produced in shoot tips. It promotes cell elongation. In phototropism, light causes auxin to move to the shaded side of the stem, causing more elongation there, bending the shoot toward light. High concentrations inhibit root growth.

Question 108medium

The hormone produced by the adrenal medulla during stress is:

  1. Adrenaline (epinephrine) — triggers 'fight-or-flight' response: increased heart rate, blood pressure, blood glucose
  2. Cortisol (adrenal cortex, long-term stress)
  3. Insulin
  4. Thyroxine
Show answer

Answer: Adrenaline (epinephrine) — triggers 'fight-or-flight' response: increased heart rate, blood pressure, blood glucose

Adrenal medulla secretes adrenaline (epinephrine) and noradrenaline in response to sudden stress. Effects (fight-or-flight): increased heart rate and blood pressure, dilated pupils, bronchodilation, increased blood glucose, reduced digestive activity. Short-term acute response. Cortisol (adrenal cortex) handles long-term stress.

Question 109easy

The full form of LASER is:

  1. Light Amplification by Stimulated Emission of Radiation
  2. Light Amplified by Solar Energy Radiation
  3. Long-range Amplified Signal Emitting Radiation
  4. Light Activated Stimulated Emission Radiation
Show answer

Answer: Light Amplification by Stimulated Emission of Radiation

LASER = Light Amplification by Stimulated Emission of Radiation. Principle: stimulated emission — an excited atom emits a photon identical to the incident photon when struck by another photon. This creates a coherent, monochromatic, collimated beam. Applications: barcode scanners, CD/DVD players, surgery, fiber optics, cutting, and holography.

Question 110medium

The phenomenon of diffraction of light proves that:

  1. Light has wave nature — waves bend around obstacles and spread through narrow openings (slit width ≈ wavelength of light)
  2. Light is made of particles
  3. Light travels in straight lines always
  4. Light cannot bend
Show answer

Answer: Light has wave nature — waves bend around obstacles and spread through narrow openings (slit width ≈ wavelength of light)

Diffraction: waves bend around obstacles or spread after passing through narrow openings (most pronounced when opening ≈ wavelength). Light shows diffraction (proving wave nature), but the effect is small because light wavelengths are tiny (400-700 nm). CD surface diffraction creates rainbow colors.

Question 111medium

Which of the following is NOT a greenhouse gas?

  1. Oxygen (O₂) and Nitrogen (N₂) — they do not absorb infrared radiation
  2. Carbon dioxide (CO₂)
  3. Methane (CH₄)
  4. Nitrous oxide (N₂O)
Show answer

Answer: Oxygen (O₂) and Nitrogen (N₂) — they do not absorb infrared radiation

Greenhouse gases absorb and re-emit infrared (thermal) radiation: CO₂, CH₄, N₂O, H₂O vapor, ozone, CFCs. O₂ and N₂ (which make up ~99% of atmosphere) do NOT absorb IR radiation — they are NOT greenhouse gases. This is why the atmosphere is transparent to incoming sunlight but traps outgoing heat.

Question 112easy

The speed of light in vacuum is approximately:

  1. 3 × 10⁸ m/s (300,000 km/s) — the fastest speed possible; light from Sun reaches Earth in ~8.3 minutes
  2. 3 × 10⁶ m/s
  3. 3 × 10¹⁰ m/s
  4. 343 m/s (that's sound)
Show answer

Answer: 3 × 10⁸ m/s (300,000 km/s) — the fastest speed possible; light from Sun reaches Earth in ~8.3 minutes

Speed of light in vacuum: c = 2.998 × 10⁸ m/s ≈ 3 × 10⁸ m/s = 300,000 km/s. Light takes: 8.3 minutes from Sun to Earth, 1.3 seconds from Moon to Earth, 4.24 years from Proxima Centauri. Speed of light is reduced in media (glass, water) — basis of refraction.

Question 113easy

The human ear can detect frequencies in the range of:

  1. 20 Hz to 20,000 Hz (20 kHz) — below 20 Hz is infrasound; above 20 kHz is ultrasound (bats, dolphins, dog whistles use ultrasound)
  2. 100 Hz to 100 kHz
  3. 1 Hz to 1,000 Hz
  4. 50 Hz to 50 kHz
Show answer

Answer: 20 Hz to 20,000 Hz (20 kHz) — below 20 Hz is infrasound; above 20 kHz is ultrasound (bats, dolphins, dog whistles use ultrasound)

Human audible range: 20 Hz (very deep bass) to 20,000 Hz (20 kHz, high-pitched). This narrows with age (presbycusis). Infrasound (<20 Hz): earthquakes, large animals, some whales. Ultrasound (>20 kHz): bats (echolocation), dolphins, medical imaging (1-20 MHz), dog whistles (~40 kHz).

Question 114easy

The layer of Earth's atmosphere where most weather phenomena occur is:

  1. Troposphere (0-12 km altitude) — contains ~75% of atmospheric mass, all water vapor; temperature decreases with altitude
  2. Stratosphere (12-50 km) — where ozone layer is
  3. Mesosphere (50-80 km)
  4. Thermosphere (80-600 km)
Show answer

Answer: Troposphere (0-12 km altitude) — contains ~75% of atmospheric mass, all water vapor; temperature decreases with altitude

Troposphere: lowest atmospheric layer (0-8 km at poles, 0-16 km at equator). Contains: 75% of atmospheric mass, all water vapor and clouds, all weather events. Temperature decreases with altitude at ~6.5°C/km. Stratosphere above: weather-free, ozone layer, jets fly here for smooth flight.

Question 115medium

Isaac Newton's contribution to mathematics includes:

  1. Development of calculus (simultaneously and independently with Leibniz) — also discovered binomial theorem and made contributions to infinite series
  2. Logarithms (Napier)
  3. Coordinate geometry (Descartes)
  4. Complex numbers (Euler)
Show answer

Answer: Development of calculus (simultaneously and independently with Leibniz) — also discovered binomial theorem and made contributions to infinite series

Isaac Newton (1642-1727): Principia Mathematica (1687) — laws of motion and gravitation. Mathematics: co-invented calculus (he called it 'method of fluxions'; Leibniz's notation dx/dy is used today), generalized binomial theorem, developed infinite series. Physics: optics (white light decomposition), reflecting telescope.

Question 116easy

The discovery of X-rays was made by:

  1. Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen (1895, Germany) — accidentally discovered while experimenting with cathode ray tubes; Nobel Prize in Physics 1901 (first ever Nobel in Physics)
  2. Marie Curie
  3. Michael Faraday
  4. Thomas Edison
Show answer

Answer: Wilhelm Conrad Röntgen (1895, Germany) — accidentally discovered while experimenting with cathode ray tubes; Nobel Prize in Physics 1901 (first ever Nobel in Physics)

Wilhelm Röntgen discovered X-rays on November 8, 1895, while experimenting with a cathode ray tube — he noticed a fluorescent screen glowing even when shielded by black paper. Named 'X' as unknown rays. First Nobel Prize in Physics (1901). First X-ray image: his wife's hand, showing her wedding ring and bones.

Question 118easy

Question 119medium

A car accelerates uniformly from rest to 20 m/s in 5 seconds. If the mass of the car is 1000 kg, what is the average power developed by the engine during this period?

  1. 20 kW
  2. 40 kW
  3. 80 kW
  4. 100 kW
Show answer

Answer: 40 kW

First, calculate acceleration (a = v/t = 20/5 = 4 m/s²). Then, calculate force (F = ma = 1000 * 4 = 4000 N). Finally, calculate average power (P_avg = W/t = (F * d)/t = F * (v_avg) = 4000 * (20/2) = 4000 * 10 = 40,000 W = 40 kW).

Question 120medium

A convex lens forms a real, inverted image of an object. If the object is moved closer to the lens, but still outside the focal length, what happens to the size and position of the image?

  1. Image becomes smaller and moves closer to the lens.
  2. Image becomes larger and moves closer to the lens.
  3. Image becomes smaller and moves further from the lens.
  4. Image becomes larger and moves further from the lens.
Show answer

Answer: Image becomes larger and moves further from the lens.

As an object moves closer to a convex lens (beyond F), the real image moves further away from the lens and increases in size. This is a fundamental property of convex lenses.

Question 121medium

Two wires, A and B, are made of the same material and have the same length. Wire A has a diameter twice that of wire B. If the resistance of wire B is R, what is the resistance of wire A?

  1. R/4
  2. R/2
  3. 2R
  4. 4R
Show answer

Answer: R/4

Resistance R is inversely proportional to the square of the diameter (R ∝ 1/d²). Since diameter of A is twice that of B, its area is four times (π(2d)² = 4πd²). Therefore, resistance of A will be R/4.

Question 122medium

  1. The image is virtual, erect, and magnified.
  2. The image is real, inverted, and diminished.
  3. The image is real, inverted, and of the same size as the object.
  4. The image is virtual, erect, and of the same size as the object.
Show answer

Answer: The image is real, inverted, and of the same size as the object.

When an object is placed at the center of curvature (C) of a concave mirror, the image formed is real, inverted, and has the same size as the object. The image also forms at C.

Question 124hard

A satellite orbits the Earth in a circular path at an altitude where the gravitational acceleration is g/4 (where g is the acceleration due to gravity at the Earth's surface). If the Earth's radius is R, what is the orbital speed of the satellite?

  1. √(gR/2)
  2. √(gR/4)
  3. √(gR/3)
  4. √(2gR)
Show answer

Answer: √(gR/3)

At altitude h, g' = GM/(R+h)^2. Since g' = g/4, (R+h)^2 = 4R^2, so h = R. Orbital speed v = √(GM/(R+h)) = √(gR^2/(2R)) = √(gR/2). Question 125hard

A block of mass 'm' is released from rest at the top of a frictionless inclined plane of height 'h' and angle 'θ'. At the bottom, it enters a rough horizontal surface with a coefficient of kinetic friction 'μ'. If the block travels a distance 'd' on the rough surface before coming to rest, what is the value of 'd'?

  1. h / (μ cos θ)
  2. h / μ
  3. h sin θ / μ
  4. h / (μ tan θ)
Show answer

Answer: h / μ

By conservation of energy, potential energy at height 'h' is converted to kinetic energy at the bottom, which is then dissipated by friction. mgh = μmgd, thus d = h/μ.

Question 126hard

An ideal gas undergoes an adiabatic expansion, decreasing its temperature by 200K. If the initial pressure was P_0 and the volume doubled during the expansion, what is the final pressure in terms of P_0? (Assume γ = 1.4 for the gas)

  1. P_0 / (2^1.4)
  2. P_0 / (2^0.4)
  3. P_0 * (2^1.4)
  4. P_0 / 2
Show answer

Answer: P_0 / (2^1.4)

For an adiabatic process, P_1V_1^γ = P_2V_2^γ. Given V_2 = 2V_1, so P_2 = P_1 * (V_1/V_2)^γ = P_0 * (1/2)^1.4.

Question 131medium

If the frequency of a wave is doubled while its speed remains constant, what happens to its wavelength?

  1. It doubles
  2. It halves
  3. It remains the same
  4. It quadruples
Show answer

Answer: It halves

The relationship between speed (v), frequency (f), and wavelength (λ) is v = fλ. If v is constant and f doubles, λ must halve to maintain the equality.
